⏺ I've read the rubric and the thought-partner agent has worked it over. Here's
  my synthesis — what's strong, what concerns me, and the decisions I need from
  you.

  What's genuinely strong

  The rubric's spine is excellent and unusually rigorous for a hackathon:
  triage-not-detection as the thesis, machine-checkable gates, and the
  anti-hallucination discipline (Gate 2: re-fetch every citation, drop
  unconfirmed to rejected.json). Gates 2–5 are real, falsifiable gates. The "no
  health advice / no safe-unsafe verdict" stance is the right legal spine. Don't
  lose any of this.

  My top concerns (where I agree with the thought partner + add my own)

  1. It's a 3-day build in a 1-day costume. Two agent runtimes (build-time
  crawler + run-time Vercel agent), 4+ live sources each with their own
  auth/rate-limits/geo-joins (EPA water-by-ZIP needs a ZIP→PWSID mapping —
  nasty), plus a 3-role adversarial confidence pipeline, plus a three.js
  centerpiece. The expensive parts (§7 confidence layer) are also the least
  demo-visible. This is the #1 risk.

  2. The demo's most likely failure: a judge types their own toaster and gets a 
  blank screen. Most household items have no active recall. There's no gate for
  empty input, item-not-found, all-CONTEXT result, or source-API-down. These are
  exactly what breaks on stage.

  3. Golden-set leakage. Gates 3–6 all read from the same golden.json the
  builder tunes against — train-on-test. And 25 hand-labeled cases is a half-day
  sink unless ACT cases are sourced from real CPSC recalls (self-labeling).

  4. Gate 7 has a perverse incentive — the cheapest way to pass "every
  independent finding has confidence+caveat" is to have zero independent
  findings, which means the most expensive component goes untested and invisible
  to judges (hurting the Orchestration score).

  5. A compliance hole the text-scan misses: absence-as-safety. "No current
  recall" is compliant text, but a green checkmark or empty plan reads as
  "you're safe" — an implied health verdict. Also: every action should trace to
  a regulator's own instruction, never originate from Warden, or you've crossed
  from reporter to advisor.

  Decisions I need from you

  These shape everything downstream, so I'd rather ask than guess:

⏺ User answered Claude's questions:

     safety signaling then. as for the self labelling; AI can tackle that no?

     crawl during demo

     recommendations? → Give me a change list first

⏺ Good — those answers sharpen things. Two of your responses are pushback I want
  to engage with directly before giving the change list, because they change
  the recommendations.

  On "rethink the safety signaling"

  You're right to zero in here — this is the subtle part. The fix isn't a
  disclaimer, it's reframing the entire output from a verdict about the item to 
  a statement about the public record. Warden never says anything about the
  thing; it reports the state of the sources as of a timestamp.

  - Wrong (implied health verdict): green check, "You're safe," empty plan that
  reads as all-clear.
  - Right (record statement): "Checked CPSC, Prop 65, EPA on 2026-06-13 — no
  active recall or public action on file for this item." Neutral color, never
  green-as-safe. The signal is coverage + recency of the check, not safety of
  the object.
  - This also kills the "blank screen" demo failure: a no-findings result
  becomes a confident, informative "here's what we searched and when" card
  instead of silence.
  - Corollary I'd bake in: every action must trace to a regulator's own
  instruction (the recall notice says "stop use / get refund"). Warden quotes
  the regulator; it never originates advice. That's the line between reporter
  and advisor.

  On "AI can tackle the self-labeling"

  Mostly yes — and that removes the "25 cases is a half-day of hand-labeling"
  objection. But it does not remove the leakage risk, and the distinction
  matters:

  - ACT cases are self-labeling from ground truth, not AI judgment — a real
  active CPSC recall is ACT by definition. AI just fetches and formats. Zero
  circularity. Pull ~10-15 real recalls this way.
  - The trap: if the same model reasoning that tiers findings at runtime also
  generates the golden labels, you're grading the system with its own answer
  key. 90% match proves nothing.
  - The fix (keeps AI doing the work): (a) ground labels in ground-truth signals
  wherever possible (real recall → ACT, real Prop 65 entry → CONTEXT); (b) have
  a separate labeler agent in a fresh context produce the answer key, not the
  runtime tiering logic; (c) hold out a slice the builder never tunes on; (d)
  human spot-checks a sample of the conditional/ADDRESS cases (those are real
  judgment calls). So: AI for volume, independence + holdout + ground-truth for
  trust.

  On live crawl during demo

  Respected — it's more authentic and impressive. But it makes Gate 8 (no-hang +
  fallback) and citation-freshness the load-bearing gates. I've added
  guardrails to the list rather than fighting the choice.

  ---
  Proposed change list for rubric.md (for your approval — no edits made yet)

  A. New gates (the "embarrassing live failure" set)

  - Gate 9 — Empty/malformed input: {items:[]} and garbage strings return
  schema-valid JSON, never a 500.
  - Gate 10 — No-findings is a record statement, not silence: an item with no
  hazards returns the neutral "checked [sources] as of <date>, nothing on file"
  card. Verifier confirms no empty array renders as blank/green.
  - Gate 11 — All-CONTEXT result is coherent: if every finding is suppressed, UI
  shows "nothing actionable; N suppressed items available," not a blank plan.
  - Gate 12 — Source-down degrades, not errors: if a live source returns
  non-200/times out at run time, fall back to precomputed + label the gap; still
  return valid JSON. (Load-bearing given live-crawl choice.)
  - Gate 13 — Pre-demo smoke check (T-30min): seeded basket produces ≥1 of each
  tier; every demo citation returns 200; cold-start latency under budget.

  B. Tighten existing gates

  - Gate 1: pin an explicit example payload + example dossier in the rubric so
  "valid" isn't a guess.
  - Gate 2: define "confirmed" concretely — cited URL returns 200 and the
  hazard_type + item identifier appear in fetched content (not a soft LLM
  grade).
  - Gate 4: add a data flag is_ubiquitous: bool (sourced from the Prop 65 list)
  so the check is mechanical: is_ubiquitous=true ⇒ tier=CONTEXT unless non-null 
  condition.
  - Gate 7: require ≥1 independent finding in the golden set so the confidence
  layer actually fires (else it's untested + invisible to judges).
  - Gate 8: pin a hard number — runtime agent returns within N seconds (suggest
  8s) or returns precomputed-only; verifier tests a forced-timeout path returns
  valid JSON.

  C. Safety-signaling rewrite (§7 Compliance)

  - Reframe output as record-state, not verdict: explicit "no green/safe
  iconography; absence uses neutral 'no action on file as of <date>' framing."
  - Compliance scan explicitly covers all schema fields (severity_basis, caveat,
  action), not just visible prose.
  - action provenance rule: every action traces to a source/regulator
  instruction; Warden originates none.
  - Adversarial skeptic explicitly hunts implied causation (chemical presence
  next to "Strong evidence" reading as harm), not just banned phrases.
  - Settlement language: "a settlement exists; eligibility criteria per claim
  site" — not "you qualify."

  D. Golden set (§4) — AI-labeled but leakage-proof

  - Split into golden_dev.json (builder tunes) and golden_holdout.json
  (verifier-only). Gate 3 runs on holdout.
  - ACT cases sourced from real CPSC recalls (self-labeling from ground truth).
  - Labels generated by a separate labeler agent in fresh context, not the
  runtime tiering logic; human spot-check on conditional cases.
  - Verifier generates 3–5 fresh real-recall cases at verify time to test
  generalization, not memorization.

  E. Demo guardrails for live crawl (new subsection)

  - Aggressive caching layer in front of every source; rate-limit Warden's own
  calls.
  - Seeded demo basket (guaranteed one-of-each-tier) one click away as the safe
  path; judges can still type their own.
  - Pre-warm the Vercel function before judging.

  F. Orchestration gate (judging alignment)

  - Gate 14: confidence pipeline produces a per-claim record showing distinct
  prosecutor/skeptic positions + adjudicator resolution — makes the most
  expensive component visible to judges and testable.

  ---
  One open item: you didn't land on a scope cut. Given you want live crawl +
  full confidence pipeline, my honest read is the schedule is tight — I'd still
  demote EPA-water-by-ZIP (the geo-join is the nastiest integration) to a
  stretch stub and keep CPSC + Prop 65 + the confidence layer as the spine. But
  that's your call.

  Want me to apply A–F to rubric.md? And should I drop EPA-water to stretch, or
  keep it in the core?

⏺ Agent "Investigate and set up OpenViking tracking" completed · 52s

⏺ The OpenViking setup agent came back with a finding worth flagging
  immediately: OpenViking is not an issue tracker. It's an open-source context 
  database for AI agents (memory/resource/skill store with vector retrieval)
  from ByteDance/Volcengine — it has no concept of issues, tickets, or status,
  and it won't even start without an embedding-model API key + a VLM API key. So
  it's a mismatch for "track open issues / big picture," though it could serve
  a different role (shared long-term memory across our agents).

  I created a zero-dependency tracker in its place and will ask you about
  OpenViking's real use below.

  ---
  Warden — User Story & the Money Shot

  The user story (one breath)

  Maya, 34, new parent, renting an older home. She's read enough to be anxious
  but has no way to act — recalls, water-quality breaches, chemical listings,
  and open settlements are all public, but smeared across a dozen agencies in
  formats nobody tracks. Scanner apps made it worse: every product screamed Prop
  65, so she learned to ignore all of it. She doesn't want a score or a 
  lecture. She wants to know: of everything I own, what actually deserves my 
  attention this week — and prove it.

  She types in her space heater, a crib, her ZIP, "infant at home, unfiltered
  tap." Fifteen seconds later Warden hands her one ranked plan, not a feed:
  - 🔴 ACT — Her exact heater model is under an active CPSC recall. Stop use, 
  here's the refund link — with the recall notice as the receipt.
  - 🟠 ADDRESS — Her water system breached a limit and she drinks unfiltered tap
  — the condition is stated; an adult on filtered water wouldn't see this tier.
  - ⚪ CONTEXT (suppressed) — The crib's generic Prop 65 sticker, folded away as
  noise, available on request.

  Every line has a re-fetched citation. Nothing says "safe." Nothing says
  "unhealthy." It's the state of the public record about her stuff, timestamped
  — and that honesty is exactly why she'd trust it.

  Where the value actually is

  The detection is commodity — anyone can hit the CPSC API. The defensible 
  product is triage + honest confidence + restraint:
  1. Calibrated severity — ranks by what matters to this person in this context.
  2. Noise suppression — the thing competitors get wrong; ubiquitous warnings
  demoted to CONTEXT so the real signal survives.
  3. Provenance over vibes — every claim re-fetched and confirmed at the
  locator, or it's dropped to rejected.json.
  4. Graded independent evidence — the prosecutor/skeptic/adjudicator pipeline
  turns "a study says…" into a defensible confidence tier.
  5. Discipline as a feature — refusing the health verdict is what makes it
  credible, not what limits it.

  The money shot (what wins the room)

  The demo's peak is a single 15-second moment, staged in three beats:

  ▎ Beat 1 — the shield. The three.js invisible dome sits over Maya's home, calm
  ▎ and translucent. This is the emotional anchor: protection made visible.
  ▎
  ▎ Beat 2 — the breach. A judge (or the seeded basket) submits real items. The 
  ▎ dome reacts to a real, live-crawled CPSC recall — a shimmer/fracture at the 
  ▎ ACT finding — while a dozen Prop 65 stickers visibly get swept into the 
  ▎ CONTEXT drawer instead of alarming. The screen shows triage happening: one 
  ▎ red card rising, the noise sinking.
  ▎
  ▎ Beat 3 — the receipt. Click the ACT card → the actual recall notice, 
  ▎ re-fetched live, 200-confirmed. "We don't ask you to trust us. Here's the 
  ▎ source."

  That sequence hits all four judging axes at once:
  - Impact — a real recall on a real item, with the noise that usually buries it
  visibly suppressed.
  - Demo — the shield is the visual hook; live crawl proves it's real, not
  canned.
  - Autonomy — the build→verify→fix loop and a self-caught failure are in the
  session log; the verifier re-ran the gates in a fresh context.
  - Orchestration — the confidence pipeline is legible: prosecutor vs. skeptic
  vs. adjudicator shown per claim, and "done" is machine-checked against this
  rubric.

  The single sentence to land it: "Everyone else detects hazards and 
  over-alarms. Warden tells you the three that matter, proves each one, and 
  never pretends to be your doctor."

  Risk to protect the money shot

  The one thing that kills Beat 2 is a judge typing items with no active recall 
  → blank screen. The seeded basket (guaranteed one-of-each-tier, one click
  away) is the insurance — let judges type their own, but always have the live
  recall ready to fire.

✻ Crunched for 4m 51s

❯ does the current warden rubric allow for custom interest tracking and         
  discovery e.g "i live near an airport and military base so maybe theres PFAs" 
  shouldnt be a conern; it should be something the system does                  

⏺ Good catch — this is a real gap, and you're right that it should be a
  capability, not a worry. Let me be honest about where the rubric stands:

  No, the current rubric doesn't do this. Today, context is only a tier modifier
  — "infant at home" tilts a finding about a listed item up or down (§6).
  "Water source / region" feeds a direct EPA-by-ZIP lookup. There is no 
  mechanism for hypothesis generation: nothing takes "near an airport + military
  base," reasons "that's the classic AFFF firefighting-foam → PFAS pathway,"
  and goes investigating a hazard the user never named. The rubric even promises
  this ("surfaces what official channels haven't flagged yet") but has no
  mechanism or gate behind the promise. So adding it makes the rubric honest
  about a claim it already makes.

  The one real tension — and why it needs careful framing, not just a green
  light: discovery is exactly where hallucination and over-alarm creep back in,
  the two things §3 and §5 exist to kill. "Maybe there's PFAS!" must never
  become a claim. The design that keeps it safe:

  - A hypothesis is a reasoning artifact, never a finding. It earns a dossier
  slot only when a real source confirms it at a locator.
  - A hypothesis that finds nothing → a calm, timestamped record statement
  ("checked EPA PFAS data for your water system as of <date>; nothing on file"),
  never a speculative ADDRESS/ACT.
  - Showing "what we checked and why" is itself a trust + autonomy artifact —
  and a great demo beat — not a list of scares.

  This actually strengthens the money shot: "I live near an airport" → Warden
  reasons its way to PFAS → pulls the real local water-system data → surfaces a
  confirmed detection with a receipt, or honestly reports nothing. That's the
  autonomy story judges reward.

  Let me fold it into the rubric.

  What changed in rubric.md:
  - New §11 — Contextual discovery (hypothesis-driven investigation): Warden

  airport/military-base → AFFF → PFAS example is the worked case.

  hypothesis, pursued against a real source, resolving to a cited finding or a
  calm record statement — never a speculative alarm.
  - Anti-alarm guardrails baked in so it doesn't break the
  anti-hallucination/calibration spine: hypotheses are reasoning artifacts
  (never claims), unconfirmed → timestamped "nothing on file" statement, same
  tiering/calibration applies, presence+provenance only, and a transparent "what
  we checked and why" trail.
  - Threaded through the intro, the core-insight line, intake (§6 now accepts

  flagged as the discovery fuel).
  - Golden-set requirement: ≥2 discovery cases, including one where a plausible
  hypothesis correctly finds nothing and must stay calm — that decoy is what
  keeps discovery from regressing into the over-alarming the product exists to
  fix.

  ISSUES.md has the decision logged and a new build task (#008: the
  exposure-pathway hypothesis library — context signal → known pathway → source
  to query), and memory is updated.

  This also upgrades the demo: the strongest autonomy beat is now "I live near
  an airport" → Warden reasons its way to PFAS → pulls the real local water data
  → shows a receipt or an honest "nothing on file." That's a sharper money shot
  than a product-list match.

  One framing decision worth your eye: I scoped discovery to a curated pathway 
  library (known exposure routes) rather than fully open-ended LLM inference.
  That's the safer, more defensible path — every hypothesis traces to an
  established route, which keeps the skeptic/adjudicator honest. If you'd rather
  let the agent infer pathways freely (more impressive, higher
  hallucination/over-reach risk), say so and I'll widen §11 with the matching
  guardrails.

  → reconcile, ~8 agents on Opus). It'll produce the exact rubric edits for

  reviewed the output. You can watch live with /workflows.

  The design it's converging on (which the adversarial lenses will stress-test
  before I commit anything):

  - Two-layer grounding. Layer 1 — a search-grounded judge verifies the inferred
  pathway itself is a real, established exposure route (defaults to reject;
  ranks gov/regulatory/peer-reviewed over SEO noise), so we never investigate a
  hallucinated route. Layer 2 — your existing §3 provenance still governs
  whether the eventual finding is real.
  - Curated library stays as the precision core; open-ended LLM inference is the
  high-recall extension feeding the same judge.
  - Provenance-of-origin labeling — origin: user_listed | ai_inferred, and
  AI-inferred items carry their pathway-grounding citation, surfaced neutrally
  in the UI ("Warden investigated this on its own because [credible source]
  links it to your context") — neither scary nor second-class.
  - Ungrounded inferences → rejected, never surfaced. New golden cases include a
  tempting-but-ungrounded pathway the judge must reject.

⏺ Auto mode lets Claude handle permission prompts automatically — Claude
  checks each tool call for risky actions and prompt injection before 
  executing. Actions Claude identifies as safe are executed, while 
  actions Claude identifies as risky are blocked and Claude may try a 
  different approach. Ideal for long-running tasks. Sessions are 
  slightly more expensive. Claude can make mistakes that allow harmful 
  commands to run, it's recommended to only use in isolated 
  environments. Shift+Tab to change mode.

         +hway:{source_category, source_to_media_mechanism, environmental

         +d_allowlist_entry, established_route_quote, evidence_hash}}`. A

         +e_tier` (§7) is unchanged and **origin-blind**.

          + airport and a military base"* → Warden infers a known exposur
          +e pathway (AFFF firefighting foam → PFAS) and investigates the

      17  - **Provenance is mechanical.** Every finding carries `source.u
          rl` + `source.locator`; "confirmed" means the URL returns 200 A
          ND the fact appears at the locator. Unconfirmed → dropped to `r
          ejected`. No claim exceeds what the source states.
      18  - **Calibration over alarm.** Over-alarming is the cardinal sin
           (it's what competitors get wrong). Ubiquitous warnings ≤ CONTE
          XT; regional baselines ≤ AWARE unless a stated condition applie
          s.
      19  - **Actions trace to a source.** Every `action` quotes a regula
          tor/source instruction; Warden originates no advice.
      20 -- **Hypotheses are reasoning artifacts, never claims.** (Contex
         -tual discovery, §11.) An inferred pathway must pass a search-gr
         -ounded judge before investigation, and unconfirmed → calm recor
         -d statement, never a speculative alarm.                        
      20 +- **Hypotheses are reasoning artifacts, never claims.** (Contex
         +tual discovery, §11.) **Two gates in series:** a search-grounde
         +d, default-reject judge proves the *pathway* is a real establis
         +hed route (mechanical domain allowlist; string-linkage + anti-e
         +quivocation; agent re-derived independently) → then §3 proves t
         +he *finding*. AI-inferred items are labeled by `origin` and car
         +ry two receipts (pathway grounding + finding source). Unconfirm
         +ed → calm record statement, never a speculative alarm. Rejected
         + pathways vanish to `discovery_rejected.json` (verifier-only). 
         +Surface-capped (≤3 ai_inferred rows; empties aggregate, bottom-

⏺ Done — the open-inference design is applied, committed, and up for review.

  Milestone landed: §11 open-ended pathway inference

  The 8-agent adversarial workflow produced a genuinely rigorous design, and I
  applied it to rubric.md. The core of it:

  - Two gates in series — a search-grounded, default-reject judge proves the
  pathway is a real, established exposure route before it costs an investigation
  turn → then §3 proves the finding is real. Open inference changes what gets
  investigated, never the bar for what becomes a claim.
  - origin labeling (user_listed | curated_pathway | ai_inferred) + a discovery
  receipt, so AI-inferred items carry two citations (why-we-looked +
  what-we-found), surfaced neutrally ("Checked because of your context").
  - Mechanical, not vibes — hardcoded Tier-1/2 domain allowlist (the judge can't
  promote a source by prose), string-level linkage + anti-equivocation (granite
  countertop ≠ granitic bedrock), surface cap so calm "nothing found"
  statements can't flood the dossier.

  What makes me trust it: the three adversarial lenses earned their keep. They
  caught — and the reconcile fixed — a factually-broken negative-control example
  (the original "granite→arsenic→water" reject case is actually a real Tier-1
  route, so the judge could have legitimately grounded it; replaced with
  memory-foam-mattress→flame-retardant→water, which has no waterborne
  precedent), an "ungrounded tier" that was secretly an LLM judgment, a
  determinism gate that's physically impossible (LLMs aren't reproducible even
  at temp 0 → rescoped to the cached basket + a 5/5 live stability-reject), and
  dossier flooding. The residual tunables (allowlist, agent registry-id
  matching, N/M caps, linkage window) are logged in ISSUES.md #012 as
  "calibrate, not assert."

      155  * **INFER (wide, cost-bounded; separate context from the judge
           ).** Curated library is consulted **first**; a curated hit sho
           rt-circuits to investigation stamped `origin="curated_pathway"
           ` and **never enters the judge**. For everything else the mode
           l associates freely from *every* context signal but **cannot e
           mit a bare hazard name**: each candidate is a structured **ATS
           DR completed-exposure-pathway** object — `source_category` → `
           source_to_media_mechanism` → `environmental_media` → `point_of
           _exposure` → `exposure_route` → `receptor_population` — plus `
           trigger_signal` (verbatim intake span), `proposed_source_to_qu
           ery`, `inferred_agent`, and `inference_rationale`. `inferred_a
           gent` **must resolve to a registered identifier in a named reg
           istry — a single-substance CASRN OR a class/group id** (ATSDR 
           ToxProfile id, EPA contaminant-group id, PubChem class) so mix
           tures/classes (PFAS, AFFF, creosote, diesel exhaust) are admis
           sible — else the candidate is dropped. **The 5-slot decomposit
           ion is a STRUCTURING device, not a filter** — a fluent model f
           ills all five slots effortlessly with individually-true compon
           ents; element-wise grounding is necessary-but-grossly-insuffic
           ient and the actual gate is the **linkage** check below. Bound
           ed for §A: hard **cap of N=8** candidates after curated reserv
           ations; pre-judge **drop** of any candidate naming no register
           ed queryable Warden source, restating a listed product, or dup
           licating a curated entry; self-ranked by trigger-signal direct
           ness (verbatim span > loose proxy). Plausibility floor is **in
           tentionally low** — the judge, not inference, is the gate.
      156  
      157  * **GROUND (the gate; default-reject; search-backed; adversari
           al; fresh context).** Each surviving candidate goes to the **§
           7 prosecutor/skeptic/adjudicator** structure (not a single con
           firm pass), asking **only** *"is this proposed pathway a real,
            established exposure route in the authoritative record?"* — *
           *never** "is this user exposed" (that is §3). The judge receiv
           es **only** `trigger_signal` + the pathway STRUCTURE; `inferen
           ce_rationale` and `inferred_agent` are **WITHHELD** — the judg
           e **independently re-derives the agent** from sources, and if 
           its agent ≠ the inferrer's it **REJECTs as `agent_mismatch`** 
           (a fresh context window without withholding is cosmetic). It *
           *must run ≥1 search (incl. a SKEPTIC negative query, e.g. "is 
           X a documented source of Y in Z" / "X NOT a source of Y") and 
           fetch ≥1 source.** PASS is **mechanical, never a prose grade**
            (mirrors §3) and requires ALL of:

  Quick answer to your question while I survey the env:

  ▎ Can't Vercel replace Supabase?

  Not directly — Vercel is compute/hosting and no longer offers its own database
  (Vercel Postgres/KV were discontinued). What it offers instead is Neon 
  Postgres via the Vercel Marketplace (auto-injected env vars, tight
  integration). So the real choice is Supabase Postgres vs Neon Postgres — both
  are plain Postgres, interchangeable for us (we only need a table the harness
  writes and the runtime reads; we don't use Supabase auth/realtime/storage).
  Plan: keep "Postgres" as the abstraction, run it locally for v1, and at deploy
  time pick Supabase-cloud or Neon-via-Vercel (Neon is the lower-friction
  choice if we deploy on Vercel). That keeps us un-blocked now and flexible
  later.

  First: secure your key (gitignored, never committed) and survey what's
  installed.

⏺ Found it — the CPSC RecallTitle/ProductName params do substring (contains) 
  matching, so passing the whole multi-word item ("Fisher-Price Rock 'n Play
  Sleeper") matches nothing, but "Rock 'n Play" returns 3. I need a
  candidate-term generator (full string + significant tokens + a brand+noun
  bigram), then let triage filter relevance. Rewriting the query logic.

       6  """
       7  from __future__ import annotations
       8  
       9 +import re

         -ion"]                                                          
      14 +# CPSC params do SUBSTRING (contains) matching, AND-combined — 
         +so a whole multi-word item                                     
      15 +# ("Fisher-Price Rock 'n Play Sleeper") matches nothing. We fan
         + out short candidate terms                                     
      16 +# across these fields, merge by RecallID, and let the triage pa
         +ss filter relevance.                                           
      17 +_SEARCH_FIELDS = ["RecallTitle", "ProductName"]                
      18 +_STOP = {"the", "and", "for", "with", "from", "plus", "due", "y
         +our", "size"}                                                  
      19

      16 -def search_recalls(query: str, *, limit: int = 8, since: str = 
         -"2010-01-01",                                                  
      21 +def _candidates(item: str, *, max_terms: int = 5) -> list[str]:
      22 +    """Full string + significant single tokens + a brand+noun b
         +igram (substring-friendly)."""                                 
      23 +    item = item.strip()                                        
      24 +    toks = re.findall(r"[A-Za-z0-9'&/-]+", item)               
      25 +    sig = [t for t in toks if len(t.strip("'-&/")) >= 4 and t.l
         +ower() not in _STOP]                                           
      26 +    cands = [item, *sig]                                       
      27 +    if len(sig) >= 2:                                          
      28 +        cands.insert(1, f"{sig[0]} {sig[1]}")  # e.g. "Fisher-P
         +rice Rock"                                                     
      29 +    seen, out = set(), []                                      
      30 +    for c in cands:                                            
      31 +        k = c.lower().strip()                                  
      32 +        if k and k not in seen:                                
      33 +            seen.add(k)                                        
      34 +            out.append(c)                                      
      35 +    return out[:max_terms]

⏺ Root cause in the log: anthropic.APITimeoutError — the triage call for one
  item exceeded the 40s timeout, then retried (→ ~80s), and the uncaught
  exception 500'd the whole dossier. Three fixes: (1) fail-fast triage (no
  retry, smaller output), (2) graceful per-item degradation so one slow item
  never 500s the dossier (§9), (3) pre-seed the demo basket so the demo path is
  cached/instant. Editing:

⏺ Agent "Frontend design judge for Warden" completed · 2m 7s

⏺ The frontend judge came back with a sharp verdict — relaying the essentials:

  Current UI: C/C+. Rubric-correct semantics (tier-only severity, no
  green/all-clear, origin-blind shield, reporter-not-advisor copy — all worth
  keeping), but visually generic "dark-SaaS AI-slop": system fonts, near-black
  #0a0a0f canvas, predictable 380px-rail layout. The one nice thing (the shader)
  is hidden behind a glass panel.

  On your particle + white instinct — the judge strongly agrees on particles, 
  pushes back on literal white:
  - Particles win the metaphor decisively. A sphere reads as an object (a
  marble/bubble) — which subtly contradicts "never a verdict about a thing." A
  field of many points reads as coverage — many independent checks forming a
  watchful shell around your home. Density/agitation also encode tier far better
  than a sphere's opacity, and points degrade gracefully for perf.
  - But pure white is a rubric trap: a serene white screen with calm dots reads
  as "you're safe" — the exact all-clear semantics §7 forbids, sneaking in
  through the visual door. The judge's fix: a committed warm-paper "archival 
  record" light theme (#F4F1EA bone, warm ink, grain) — "an official record on a
  desk," not "a clean safe room." Calm state = quiet but fully present field in
  neutral slate (never green/warm), always with the timestamped "checked as of
  <date>."

  Concrete plan it gave: one THREE.Points GPU field (~6–9k points,
  spherical-shell+jitter, tier→density/agitation/color + an ACT "breach pulse,"
  all motion in-shader, static fallback); real font pairing (Fraunces-style
  serif display + warm sans + mono for citations/receipts — very on-thesis);
  light-mode dossier cards with tier color as the sole severity signal;
  orchestrated load reveal.

  One quick call before I build it — your word was "white," the judge says
  warm-paper for a real reason:

⏺ User answered Claude's questions:

✻ Crunched for 1m 29s

❯  /btw what about the live agent scan view?                                    
                                                                                
      Short answer: there isn't a live "agent scan" view in the build right now 
  — and it's a demo/UX enhancement, not a rubric requirement.                   
                                                                                
      What actually exists today:                                               
      - The runtime is a fast FastAPI call (CPSC + triage + Prop 65 + EPA in    
  parallel), not a visibly-streamed agent loop. The UI just shows a loading     
  state ("Checking the public record…") and then the finished dossier.          
      - The "what we checked" surfacing is after the fact: checked_sources on   
  the response, per-finding why + the cited receipt, and the timestamped record 
  statement. The three.js shield reacts to the result tier, not to a            
  scan-in-progress.                                                             
                                                                                
      How this maps to the rubric:                                              
        - The rubric's §10 orchestration visibility is satisfied by a stored,   
  inspectable per-claim record (prosecutor/skeptic/adjudicator in the           
  build-time confidence pipeline; the §11 pathway-judge legibility record) —    
  i.e., legible to a verifier/judge, not necessarily a live streaming UI. The   
  §11 "what we checked and why" trail is likewise an output artifact, not a     
  live feed.                                                                    
        - So a live agent-scan view is not a HARD gate — none of the 12 gates   
  require it. Nothing is non-compliant by lacking it.                           
                                                                                
        That said, it's a genuinely strong demo move (it dramatizes the         
  Autonomy/Orchestration story — "watch Warden reason through each source").    
  Building it would be net-new: stream progress from the Python brain (e.g.     
  SSE/messages.stream events or per-source step events) and render a step list  
  / activity log in the UI. Worth noting it's also in tension with the ≤8s      
  runtime budget — a live view is most honest paired with the                   
  build-time/precompute path (where the heavy adversarial pipeline actually     
  runs) rather than the fast runtime resolve.                                   
                                                                                
        One caveat: the UI reskin agent is still iterating, so treat the exact  
  current loading-state styling as in flux — but no live scan view was in its   
  brief (particle field + theme + UX/error fixes only), so this assessment      
  holds.                                                                        
                                                                                
  little sidechat i had with you. lets make sure the agentic run is in the      
  rubric and final product                                                      

⏺ Got it — the live agentic-scan view should be a first-class part of both the
  spec and the product. You're right it's not a current gate, but if we want it
  guaranteed in the final build, the rubric is where we lock it. Let me make it
  real.

      170  
      171  **Relationship to the curated library:** complementary, not re
           placement — **one schema, one judge, one investigation engine,
            one §3 verifier**; only the *source* of the pathway differs (
           what `origin` records). Curated stays the pre-vetted fast path
            (skips the search judge → zero extra latency, deterministic b
           asket). Two feedback loops, both human-gated: (1) an `ai_infer
           red` pathway that repeatedly grounds **and** yields §3-confirm
           ed findings is a **promotion candidate** into the curated libr
           ary **only on independent-labeler/human sign-off** (mirroring 
           §4's fresh-context labeler) — never auto-promoted from repeate
           d judge passes; promoted entries are periodically **re-judged*
           *, not trusted in perpetuity. (2) An **immutable, human-curate
           d SEED set** (never judge-promoted) is the **regression oracle
           **: every seed pathway SHOULD pass the judge, so a rejected kn
           own-real seed flags judge mis-tuning — the oracle's ground tru
           th is independent of the judge's own prior outputs.

⏺ Two "for later" tracks captured — and one has an actionable piece now. Let me
  address the design question you posed, set up the UX pairing correctly around
  the in-flight work, and persist the vision.

  The adversarial-LLM-filter idea (you asked me to come up with one) — this
  extends the §11 judge we already specced, tuned for the
  snappy-enrollment/initiatives flow as a propose → prosecute → declare loop:

  1. Propose (Sonnet, cheap, high-recall): from the parsed enrollment (location
  + items + lifestyle), Sonnet emits candidate initiatives as structured
  exposure-pathway hypotheses — "near airport → AFFF firefighting foam → PFAS →
  groundwater/well." These are hypotheses, never claims.
  2. Prosecute (adversarial, default-reject): each candidate goes to a skeptic
  pass whose job is to kill it — handed the pathway without the proposer's
  rationale (independence), it must run a falsifying search ("is X NOT a
  documented source of Y") and may only let it survive if a Tier-1/2 
  authoritative source affirmatively attests the whole route (the §11 mechanical
  allowlist + string-linkage + anti-equivocation). Uncertain → rejected. The
  novelty: it's a self-falsification debate, not a confirmation pass — survival
  requires the refutation attempt to fail.
  3. Declare: survivors are labeled "Checked because of your context" (neutral
  chip, origin=ai_inferred) with two separate receipts — why we looked (the
  grounding) vs what we found (§3). Rejected initiatives vanish to
  discovery_rejected.json, never shown. That's your "declared as such"
  requirement.
  This is exactly what a warden-discovery skill should encapsulate
  (propose→prosecute→declare) — good call; I've logged it.

  On the UX agents — there's a real constraint: the live-scan agent is editing 
  the frontend right now, so I can't have a UX coder touch page.tsx
  simultaneously (merge hell). So I'm starting the UX designer agent now
  (design-only — it produces a spec/mockups, zero code conflict) and queuing the
  UX coder to implement from that spec once the live-scan work lands. Both use
  the frontend-design skill; designer informs coder, exactly as you said.

  (the rubric's "settlement to claim → ACT" path). That's tracked as #018 and

  stability, and settlement-eligibility borders on legal advice (so the rubric's
  wording is "a settlement exists; eligibility per the claim site," never "you
  qualify").

  TODO. Let me capture both refinements so they survive the reset.

❯ i had an idea. lets help the user list out possible stuff they own with a clever autocomnplete. it asks for age, single status, partenr, car etc. can you think of a clever way to use LLMs to speed up the enrollment process? lets also keep a "recently viewed" DB of baskets and info for a given particular user. 

⏺ Love this — it turns enrollment from "type a list" into "confirm a smart
  guess," which is the biggest friction win available. Quick proposal, then I'll
  capture it (the current goal's two build agents — flow-sight +
  judge-inspection + friction polish — are mid-flight, so this is
  enrollment-rework territory we queue, not interrupt).

  Clever LLM-driven enrollment

  The core move: profile → predicted basket. Ask a handful of light, tappable
  questions (household: solo / partner / kids; home: rent/own + rough age; a
  car?; ZIP + the unfiltered-tap toggle). Then Sonnet predicts the inventory you
  likely own and renders it as accept/reject chips — "You probably have… space 
  heater crib Peloton gas range extension cords power banks — tap to keep." One
  tap per item beats typing, and the model is biased toward recall-prone 
  categories (infant gear, heaters, batteries, treadmills) so the predicted
  basket is both realistic and high-signal.

  Three LLM roles, layered for snappiness:
  1. Typeahead autocomplete — instant suggestions from a static dictionary of
  recall-prone brands/categories (zero-latency), with a debounced Haiku call
  only to canonicalize messy input ("pelo" → "Peloton Tread+", "my baby's bed" →
  "infant crib/sleeper").
  2. Profile → predicted basket — one Sonnet call after the questions → ranked
  likely-possessions + why each matters (maps to a hazard category). Fast
  (single call), and it's the "wow."
  3. Free-text fallback — "just tell me about your place" → Sonnet parses items
  + context (the #037 parse).

  One compliance line to hold: these stay possession-prediction proxies, never
  health inference. "Kids?" → predicts cribs/car seats ✅. We avoid
  age-as-health-proxy / anything medical (the rubric's non-medical-proxy rule).
  The profile also doubles as the §11 discovery context (ZIP + "near airport" +
  "old home" → PFAS/lead initiatives).

  Recently-viewed baskets DB (per user)

  Pairs perfectly with the Clerk auth (already scaffolded, inert). Keyed by
  Clerk userId: persist each audit (basket + a dossier snapshot + date). On
  return, show "recently viewed" so they re-run in one click — and the killer
  feature it unlocks: "since your last audit, a new recall was filed on your 
  space heater" — re-engagement + the monitoring angle the rubric promises
  ("official channels are slow"). Storage = the SQLite cache now →
  Postgres/Supabase at deploy.

  Capturing both so they survive:

❯ keyboard mode: lets change the form for inputs: user types in a box. autodetected commas, "and"s etc mark end of a word. user can just type continuously as stream of thought without thinking too much about it. 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                    
  for mobile: be creative with the low friction LLM input.                                                                                                                                                          
⏺ Both captured as concrete enrollment-input requirements — this is the input
  side of the rework (the current frontend agent is on the results side, so I
  won't bolt it on mid-flight; it goes to the UX coder / §42 enrollment build).

  Desktop "keyboard mode" (stream-of-thought): one input box, no "one per line"
  rule — the user just types continuously and commas, "and", semicolons, line 
  breaks, even a pause auto-commit each item into a removable chip as they go,
  so they watch their basket build without thinking about format. Sonnet
  canonicalizes each chip in the background ("pelo" → "Peloton Tread+"). Zero
  friction, zero rules to learn.

  Mobile — creative low-friction LLM input. A couple of ideas, since you invited
  creativity:
  - Voice-first: "Just say what you've got." Tap-and-hold to talk →
  speech-to-text → Sonnet parses the spoken stream into chips you confirm. On a
  phone, talking beats typing by a mile — and it pairs naturally with the
  stream-of-thought model (you ramble, it chips).
  - Watch-it-build chips: same auto-delimit as desktop, but chips pop in under
  the field as you dictate/type — immediate, tangible feedback.
  - Smart paste: paste an order/receipt → parse to chips.
  - (Deliberately not camera/photo scan — the rubric bars photo input.)

  Recommend voice + auto-chipping as the mobile hero. Capturing it:

❯ also wba the independent source? adverarial checks? inspector for adcversarial checks? 

⏺ Good thread to pull — these are the rubric's "act two," and they connect.
  Honest status:

  1. Independent source (§7 confidence layer) — not built. Today every finding
  is from a regulatory source (CPSC/EPA/Prop 65). The independent layer (Exa +
  OpenAlex + Semantic Scholar, grading evidence: regulatory-confirmed >
  meta-analysis > single study > preprint > NGO > journalism > anecdote) is the
  differentiator and it's gated on keys — Exa (#002), OpenAlex free key (#015),
  and the Semantic Scholar gmail-rejection decision (#014).

  2. Adversarial checks — the rubric has two adversarial mechanisms, and the
  true adversarial layer isn't built yet:
  - §7 prosecutor/skeptic/adjudicator (grades independent evidence) — needs the
  independent sources above → not built.
  - §11 grounding judge (the propose→prosecute→declare pathway filter,
  default-reject + falsification search) — the "next major build" I just queued.
  - What IS live and inspectable today is the mechanical adjudication: the §3
  re-fetch-at-locator confirm + the compliance/banned-token scan +
  action-fidelity + the dropped-candidates list. That's deterministic gating,
  not a multi-role debate.

  3. Inspector for adversarial checks — the Inspector shipping now surfaces
  those mechanical checks (matched-at-locator / compliance / action-traced /
  confirmed). It's the right surface to extend: when the §11 pathway judge + §7
  confidence layer land, the Inspector grows to show the adversarial debate —
  prosecutor vs. skeptic vs. adjudicator, the grounding judge's falsification
  search + accept/reject, and the two receipts (why-we-looked vs what-we-found).
  Same panel, deeper content.

  The single unlock: a search/research API powers both — the §7 evidence grading
  and the §11 grounding judge's "must run a falsifying search" step. That's
  Exa. So to build the adversarial/independent-source layer I need:
  - Exa API key (#002) — the big one (powers §7 + §11 grounding),
  - OpenAlex free key (#015) — instant, scholarly tier grading,
  - a call on Semantic Scholar (#014) — it rejects gmail; institutional email,
  or accept the cached-fallback path?

  This is the "ping me when APIs are needed" moment from your goal. If you drop

✻ Cooked for 2m 22s

❯ for later: lets think how to better animate the background sphere swarm e.g   
  loading etc. lets also think on the idea of invisible shield rather than just 
  a naive swarm sphere. come up with ideas                                      

⏺ Love this direction — "swarm sphere" is a placeholder; "invisible shield" is
  the actual idea and it should behave like one. Here's a menu, organized around
  one core principle, then states, then the structural moves that make it read
  as a shield instead of a ball.

  The core principle: a shield is invisible until something touches it

  A force field you can't see — until a threat hits it and it ripples, flares,
  and reveals its shape at the point of contact. That single idea makes
  "invisible shield" literal and gives every state a reason to animate:

  - Nothing wrong → you barely see it. Sparse, calm, slow-breathing field. The
  invisibility is the feature ("all quiet").
  - Something detected → it reveals itself exactly where the threat is — a
  localized bloom, ripple, or rim-flare. The shield becomes visible in 
  proportion to the hazard.

  That's the through-line. Everything below hangs off it.

  The four states, as behaviors

  ┌─────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │      State      │                    Shield behavior                    │
  ├─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Idle / NONE     │ Slow "breathing" expansion/contraction + faint patrol │
  │ (slate)         │  drift. Never dead — it's watching. Occasional slow   │
  │                 │ sweep so the eye knows it's alive.                    │
  ├─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Scanning /      │ Active vigilance — see loading ideas below. The       │
  │ loading         │ shield is "searching its own surface."                │
  ├─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ AWARE / CONTEXT │ Field tightens & converges slightly, cool glow rises  │
  │  (steel-blue)   │ — attention focusing, not yet alarmed.                │
  ├─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │                 │ A localized watch-zone: particles cluster + warm at   │
  │ ADDRESS (amber) │ one region of the shell (the issue has a location on  │
  │                 │ the shield), rest stays calm.                         │
  ├─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │                 │ The membrane ruptures: a visible puncture where       │
  │ ACT (red +      │ particles scatter outward, a shockwave ring, red      │
  │ breach)         │ Fresnel flare at the breach point. "Something got     │
  │                 │ through — act." This is the money-shot frame.         │
  └─────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  Loading / scanning — tie the animation to the live agent (on-thesis)

  You already stream ScanEvents (§12). Make the shield be the telemetry instead
  of a generic spinner:

  1. Sonar pings. Each source-check event (CPSC → EPA → FDA → Prop65…) emits a
  ripple ring that travels across the shell. The user literally watches the
  agent sweep its sensors.
  2. Lighthouse/radar sweep. A wedge of brightened particles rotates the
  perimeter; one pass ≈ one source queried. Reads instantly as "keeping watch."
  3. Recruitment particles. On each query, a few particles peel off, travel out
  to a node (the source), and return carrying brightness — visualizing "reach
  out to CPSC, pull data back."
  4. Progress arc. A thin arc traces the equator as sources complete — quiet
  progress without a bar.
  5. Settle on result. When the scan resolves, the field redistributes into its 
  result tier — calm if clear, breach if ACT. Loading → outcome is one
  continuous motion, no cut.
  6. Dossier handoff. Instead of gray skeleton cards, a few particles detach and
  hover where each finding card will mount, then the card crystallizes from
  them — background and content feel like one system.

  Making it read as a shield, not a ball (structural)

  1. Fresnel membrane. Shade by view-angle so the rim glows and the face is
  faint → reads as a translucent dome/force-field, not a solid sphere. Biggest
  single win for the "shield" feel.
  2. Negative-space core. Particles avoid a clear central void — the protected
  thing (your home/you) is defined by what the shield surrounds. The shield
  guards an emptiness, which is the point.
  3. Twin shells. A sparse outer "sensor perimeter" + a denser inner "core,"
  with guarded space between them.
  4. Faint geodesic lattice. Distribute on a subdivided icosphere (not random
  noise) so it looks engineered — a barrier, not dust.
  5. Pushable surface. Cursor/scroll dents the membrane locally with a ripple
  (like pressing a soap film) — proves on contact that it's a responsive
  surface, not decoration.

  On-thesis binding (optional, strong)

  Let particles mean something: swarm density grows with your basket size;
  during scan, particles brighten in waves matching the real event stream; a
  confirmed finding "freezes" one particle into a fixed, cited point. Then the
  visual isn't garnish — it's the audit, rendered.

  ---
  My recommended hero combo for v1 of this: Fresnel membrane + negative-space
  core (structure) → sonar-ping loading driven by ScanEvents → breach rupture on
  ACT. That trio sells "invisible shield" with the least new machinery and
  reuses the stream you already have. Perf stays safe — it's shader uniforms +
  per-particle attributes on the existing THREE.Points, device-aware count, with
  the static fallback untouched.

  Capturing this as a backlog note so "for later" is real:

⏺ Both tracker edits landed (§11/#038 marked verified, #049 captures your
  auto-discovery idea). Now addressing your two messages.

  On "Anything nearby?" → automated self-discovery

  Your instinct is right, and it's the most on-thesis change on that screen. The
  whole pitch is "things you'd never think to look up" — but a blank
  chip-picker only works if the user already suspects "military base → maybe
  PFAS." That defeats the discovery value and adds friction. Warden should infer
  the nearby layer from location, not ask.

  The clean synthesis (so we don't lose consent or the ux-coder's screen):
  auto-discover from ZIP → pre-fill the chips as a confirmation, not a blank 
  prompt. "Warden sees a former Air Force base 3 mi away and 2 TRI facilities —
  uncheck any that don't apply." Same screen, but it arrives already answered.

  Mechanically, auto-detected proximity becomes trigger signals feeding the 
  exact same §11 propose→ground→judge pipeline — so auto-discovery raises recall
  of what we check, and the default-reject grounding judge still enforces
  precision. No safety regression.

  Two honest caveats:
  - Hybrid, not pure auto. Some signals aren't geocodable — recent renovation
  (behavioral), confirmed well water (you already have a toggle). Keep a tiny
  optional escape hatch for those; auto-discover everything location-derivable
  (airports via FAA, bases + DoD/EPA PFAS-AFFF site lists, EPA FRS/TRI/Superfund
  by lat-lon radius, Census tract year-built → pre-1978 lead estimate).
  - It's a backend build (geospatial radius queries + a source-recon pass like
  we did for SOURCES.md) + a small UI change. I'd sequence it after the current 
  UX rework lands so it doesn't collide with the running ux-coder.

  Captured as #049 (P1). I won't build it now (ux-coder is live on that screen)
  — say the word and I'll kick off the geo-source recon when the UX pass merges.

  cleanly:

❯ >                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              
  You already stream ScanEvents (§12). Make the shield be the telemetry instead of a generic spinner:                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 
  1. Sonar pings. Each source-check event (CPSC → EPA → FDA → Prop65…) emits a ripple ring that travels across the shell. The user literally watches the agent sweep its sensors.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                
  2. Lighthouse/radar sweep. A wedge of brightened particles rotates the perimeter; one pass ≈ one source queried. Reads instantly as "keeping watch."                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  3. Recruitment particles. On each query, a few particles peel off, travel out to a node (the source), and return carrying brightness — visualizing "reach out to CPSC, pull data back."                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        
  4. Progress arc. A thin arc traces the equator as sources complete — quiet progress without a bar.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             
  5. Settle on result. When the scan resolves, the field redistributes into its result tier — calm if clear, breach if ACT. Loading → outcome is one continuous motion, no cut.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  
  6. Dossier handoff. Instead of gray skeleton cards, a few particles detach and hover where each finding card will mount, then the card crystallizes from them — background and content feel like one system.                                                                                                                                                                                                                   
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 
  Making it read as a shield, not a ball (structural)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 
  1. Fresnel membrane. Shade by view-angle so the rim glows and the face is faint → reads as a translucent dome/force-field, not a solid sphere. Biggest single win for the "shield" feel.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       
  2. Negative-space core. Particles avoid a clear central void — the protected thing (your home/you) is defined by what the shield surrounds. The shield guards an emptiness, which is the point.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                
  3. Twin shells. A sparse outer "sensor perimeter" + a denser inner "core," with guarded space between them.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    
  4. Faint geodesic lattice. Distribute on a subdivided icosphere (not random noise) so it looks engineered — a barrier, not dust.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               
  5. Pushable surface. Cursor/scroll dents the membrane locally with a ripple (like pressing a soap film) — proves on contact that it's a responsive surface, not decoration.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 
  On-thesis binding (optional, strong)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 
  Let particles mean something: swarm density grows with your basket size; during scan, particles brighten in waves matching the real event stream; a confirmed finding "freezes" one particle into a fixed, cited point. Then the visual isn't garnish — it's the audit, rendered.                                                                                                                                              
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 
  ---                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            
  My recommended hero combo for v1 of this: Fresnel membrane + negative-space core (structure) → sonar-ping loading driven by ScanEvents → breach rupture on ACT. That trio sells "invisible shield" with the least new machinery and reuses the stream you already have. Perf stays safe — it's shader uniforms + per-particle attributes on the existing THREE.Points, device-aware count, with the static fallback untouched. 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 
  Capturing this as a backlog note so "for later" is real:                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 
  add this to rubric as well. should be worked upon

⏺ Found the gap — and it's a clean frontend fix. The brain consumes boolean
  flags (near_military_base: true, etc. — confirmed working in my flagship
  curl), but lib/enroll.ts:181 sends the chip labels as a proximity array
  (["military base", …]) and never sets the flag keys the brain triggers on. So
  selecting "military base" in the new "Anything nearby?" UI does nothing —
  discovery only half-fires off ZIP, and the curated AFFF→PFAS pathway (which
  keys on near_military_base/near_airport) never triggers. That's exactly why
  the ux-coder saw "0 discovery chips" live.

  context, so I map labels→flags precisely:

  flags. The brain serializes the whole context (so free-text still helps
